					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Geographic region in West Asia</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the geographical region. For the political entity, see <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">State of Palestine</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p><p><b>Palestine</b><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;i&#93;</a></sup> is a geographical region in <a href="/wiki/West_Asia" title="West Asia">West Asia</a>. Situated in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Levant" title="Southern Levant">Southern Levant</a>, it is usually considered to include <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">State of Palestine</a>, though some definitions also include parts of northwestern <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>. Other historical names for the region include <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Promised_Land" title="Promised Land">Promised Land</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Israel" title="Land of Israel">Land of Israel</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a>.
</p><p>The first written records referring to Palestine emerged in the 12th-century BCE <a href="/wiki/Twentieth_Dynasty_of_Egypt" title="Twentieth Dynasty of Egypt">Twentieth Dynasty of Egypt</a>, which used the term <i>Peleset</i> for the neighboring people or land. In the 8th century BCE, the <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrians</a> referred to the region as <i>Palashtu</i> or <i>Pilistu</i>. In the <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic period</a>, these names were carried over into Greek, appearing in the <i><a href="/wiki/Histories_(Herodotus)" title="Histories (Herodotus)">Histories</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a> as <i>Palaistine</i>. In 6&#160;CE, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> established a province over the area known as <a href="/wiki/Judaea_(Roman_province)" title="Judaea (Roman province)">Judaea</a>, then in 132 CE (the time of the <a href="/wiki/Bar_Kokhba_revolt" title="Bar Kokhba revolt">Bar Kokhba revolt</a>) formed it into <a href="/wiki/Syria_Palaestina" title="Syria Palaestina">Syria Palaestina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELehmann1998_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELehmann1998-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In 390, during the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> period, the region was split into the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Prima" title="Palaestina Prima">Palaestina Prima</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Secunda" title="Palaestina Secunda">Palaestina Secunda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Salutaris" title="Palaestina Salutaris">Palaestina Tertia</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Levant" title="Muslim conquest of the Levant">Muslim conquest of the Levant</a> in the 630s, the military district of <a href="/wiki/Jund_Filastin" title="Jund Filastin">Jund Filastin</a> was established. While Palestine's boundaries have changed throughout history, it has generally comprised the southern portion of regions such as <a href="/wiki/Southern_Syria" title="Southern Syria">Syria</a> or the Levant. It also conceptually overlaps with several terms of <a href="/wiki/Judeo-Christian" title="Judeo-Christian">Judeo-Christian</a> tradition, including Canaan, the Promised Land, the Land of Israel, and the Holy Land.
</p><p>As the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, the region has a tumultuous history as a crossroads for religion, culture, commerce, and politics. In the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, it was inhabited by the Canaanites; the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> saw the emergence of <a href="/wiki/History_of_ancient_Israel_and_Judah" title="History of ancient Israel and Judah">Israel and Judah</a>, two related kingdoms inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">Israelites</a>. It has since come under the sway of various empires, including the <a href="/wiki/Neo-Assyrian_Empire" title="Neo-Assyrian Empire">Neo-Assyrian Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Neo-Babylonian_Empire" title="Neo-Babylonian Empire">Neo-Babylonian Empire</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Persian Empire</a>. Revolts by the region's <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> against <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hellenistic">Hellenistic</a> rule brought a brief period of regional independence under the <a href="/wiki/Hasmonean_dynasty" title="Hasmonean dynasty">Hasmonean dynasty</a>, which ended with its gradual incorporation into the Roman Empire (later the Byzantine Empire). 
</p><p>In the 7th century, Palestine was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">Rashidun Caliphate</a>, ending Byzantine rule in the region; Rashidun rule was succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid Caliphate</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimid Caliphate</a>. Following the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">Kingdom of Jerusalem</a>, which had been established through the <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusades</a>, the population of Palestine became predominantly <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslim</a>. In the 13th century, it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate" title="Mamluk Sultanate">Mamluk Sultanate</a>, and after 1516, part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, it was captured by the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Sinai_and_Palestine_campaign" title="Sinai and Palestine campaign">Sinai and Palestine campaign</a>. Between 1919 and 1922, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> created the <a href="/wiki/Mandate_for_Palestine" title="Mandate for Palestine">Mandate for Palestine</a>, which directed the region to be under British administration as <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Mandatory Palestine</a>. Tensions between Jews and <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> escalated into the <a href="/wiki/1948_Palestine_war" title="1948 Palestine war">1947â1949 Palestine war</a>, which ended with the remaining territory of the former British Mandate post the creation of <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Transjordan</a> in 1946 divided between Israel vis-Ã -vis Jordan (<a href="/wiki/Jordanian_annexation_of_the_West_Bank" title="Jordanian annexation of the West Bank">in the West Bank</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> (<a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Gaza_Strip_by_the_United_Arab_Republic" title="Occupation of the Gaza Strip by the United Arab Republic">in the Gaza Strip</a>); later developments in the <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict" title="ArabâIsraeli conflict">ArabâIsraeli conflict</a> culminated in <a href="/wiki/Israeli-occupied_territories" title="Israeli-occupied territories">Israel's occupation of both territories</a>, which has been among the core issues of the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="IsraeliâPalestinian conflict">IsraeliâPalestinian conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReuters:_recognition2012_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReuters:_recognition2012-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiskin2012_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiskin2012-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAP2013_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAP2013-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_the_name">History of the name</span></h2>

/></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">The name is found throughout recorded history. Examples of <a href="/wiki/Cartography_of_Palestine" title="Cartography of Palestine">historical maps of Palestine</a> are shown above: (1) <a href="/wiki/Pomponius_Mela" title="Pomponius Mela">Pomponius Mela</a> (Latin, c.&#160;43 CE); (2) <a href="/wiki/Notitia_Dignitatum" title="Notitia Dignitatum">Notitia Dignitatum</a> (Latin, c.&#160;410 CE); (3) <a href="/wiki/Tabula_Rogeriana" title="Tabula Rogeriana">Tabula Rogeriana</a> (Arabic, 1154 CE); (4) <a href="/wiki/Cedid_Atlas" title="Cedid Atlas">Cedid Atlas</a> (Ottoman Turkish, 1803 CE)</div></div></div></div>
<p>Modern archaeology has identified 12 ancient inscriptions from Egyptian and Assyrian records recording likely cognates of Hebrew <i>Pelesheth</i>. The term "Peleset" (<a href="/wiki/Transliteration_of_Ancient_Egyptian" title="Transliteration of Ancient Egyptian">transliterated</a> from <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_hieroglyphs" title="Egyptian hieroglyphs">hieroglyphs</a> as <i>P-r-s-t</i>) is found in five inscriptions referring to a neighboring people or land starting from c.&#160;1150&#160;BCE during the <a href="/wiki/Twentieth_dynasty_of_Egypt" class="mw-redirect" title="Twentieth dynasty of Egypt">Twentieth dynasty of Egypt</a>. The first known mention is at the temple at <a href="/wiki/Medinet_Habu_(temple)" class="mw-redirect" title="Medinet Habu (temple)">Medinet Habu</a> which refers to the Peleset among those who fought with <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ramesses_III" title="Ramesses III">Ramesses III</a>'s reign,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFahlbuschLochmanBromileyBarrett2005185_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFahlbuschLochmanBromileyBarrett2005185-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBreasted200124_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBreasted200124-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and the last known is 300 years later on <a href="/wiki/Padiiset%27s_Statue" title="Padiiset&#39;s Statue">Padiiset's Statue</a>. Seven known <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrian</a> inscriptions refer to the region of "Palashtu" or "Pilistu", beginning with <a href="/wiki/Adad-nirari_III" title="Adad-nirari III">Adad-nirari III</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Nimrud_Slab" title="Nimrud Slab">Nimrud Slab</a> in c.&#160;800&#160;BCE through to a <a href="/wiki/Esarhaddon%27s_Treaty_with_Ba%27al_of_Tyre" title="Esarhaddon&#39;s Treaty with Ba&#39;al of Tyre">treaty made by Esarhaddon</a> more than a century later.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESharon19884_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharon19884-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoom2006285_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoom2006285-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Neither the Egyptian nor the Assyrian sources provided clear regional boundaries for the term.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;ii&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first clear use of the term Palestine to refer to the entire area between <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> was in 5th century BCE <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">ancient Greece</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;iii&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;iv&#93;</a></sup> when <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a> wrote of a "district of Syria, called <i>PalaistinÃª</i>" (<a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Greek language">Ancient Greek</a>: <span lang="grc">Î£ÏÏÎ¯Î· á¼¡ Î Î±Î»Î±Î¹ÏÏÎ¯Î½Î· ÎºÎ±Î»ÎµÎ¿Î¼Î­Î½Î·</span>)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerodotus_3:91:1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerodotus_3:91:1-13">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> in <i><a href="/wiki/Histories_(Herodotus)" title="Histories (Herodotus)">The Histories</a></i>, which included the <a href="/wiki/Judean_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Judean mountains">Judean mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Rift_Valley" title="Jordan Rift Valley">Jordan Rift Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobson199965_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobson199965-14">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;v&#93;</a></sup> Approximately a century later, <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a> used a similar definition for the region in <i><a href="/wiki/Meteorology_(Aristotle)" title="Meteorology (Aristotle)">Meteorology</a></i>, in which he included the <a href="/wiki/Dead_Sea" title="Dead Sea">Dead Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobson199966â67_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobson199966â67-16">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Later Greek writers such as <a href="/wiki/Polemon_of_Athens" title="Polemon of Athens">Polemon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pausanias_(geographer)" title="Pausanias (geographer)">Pausanias</a> also used the term to refer to the same region, which was followed by Roman writers such as <a href="/wiki/Ovid" title="Ovid">Ovid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibullus" title="Tibullus">Tibullus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pomponius_Mela" title="Pomponius Mela">Pomponius Mela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dio_Chrysostom" title="Dio Chrysostom">Dio Chrysostom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Statius" title="Statius">Statius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plutarch" title="Plutarch">Plutarch</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Roman_Empire" title="History of the Jews in the Roman Empire">Romano-Jewish</a> writers <a href="/wiki/Philo_of_Alexandria" class="mw-redirect" title="Philo of Alexandria">Philo of Alexandria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Josephus" title="Josephus">Josephus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Robinson_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson-17">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The term was first used to denote an official province in c.&#160;135&#160;CE, when the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman authorities</a>, following the suppression of the <a href="/wiki/Bar_Kokhba_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Bar Kokhba Revolt">Bar Kokhba Revolt</a>, renamed the province of Judaea "<a href="/wiki/Syria_Palaestina" title="Syria Palaestina">Syria Palaestina</a>". There is <a href="/wiki/Circumstantial_evidence" title="Circumstantial evidence">circumstantial evidence</a> linking <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a> with the name change,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldman1996553_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldman1996553-19">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> but the precise date is not certain.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldman1996553_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldman1996553-19">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The term is generally accepted to be a cognate of the biblical name <i>Peleshet</i> (<span title="Hebrew-language text"><span lang="he" dir="rtl">×¤××©×ª</span></span> <i>PÉlÃ©sheth</i>, usually transliterated as <a href="/wiki/Philistia" title="Philistia">Philistia</a>). The term and its derivates are used more than 250 times in <a href="/wiki/Masoretic_Text" title="Masoretic Text">Masoretic</a>-derived versions of the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible">Hebrew Bible</a>, of which 10 uses are in the <a href="/wiki/Torah" title="Torah">Torah</a>, with undefined boundaries, and almost 200 of the remaining references are in the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Judges" title="Book of Judges">Book of Judges</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Books_of_Samuel" title="Books of Samuel">Books of Samuel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESharon19884_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharon19884-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoom2006285_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoom2006285-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Robinson_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson-17">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis1954153_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis1954153-20">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The term is rarely used in the <a href="/wiki/Septuagint" title="Septuagint">Septuagint</a>, which used a transliteration <i>Land of Phylistieim</i> (<i>Îá¿ Ïá¿¶Î½ Î¦ÏÎ»Î¹ÏÏÎ¹ÎµÎ¯Î¼</i>), different from the contemporary Greek place name <i>PalaistÃ­nÄ</i> (<i>Î Î±Î»Î±Î¹ÏÏÎ¯Î½Î·</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobson199972â74_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobson199972â74-21">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> It also theorized to be the <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" class="mw-redirect" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of the Greek word for the Philistines and <i>palaistÃªs</i>, which means "wrestler/rival/adversary". <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENoth1939_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENoth1939-22">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> This aligns with the Greek practice of punning place names since the latter is also the <a href="/wiki/Jacob_wrestling_with_the_angel" title="Jacob wrestling with the angel">etymological meaning for Israel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobson1999&#91;&#91;Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2021&#93;&#93;&lt;sup_class=&quot;noprint_Inline-Template_&quot;_style=&quot;white-space:nowrap;&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;&#91;&#91;Wikipedia:Citing_sources&#124;&lt;span_title=&quot;This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(February_2021)&quot;&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;&#93;&#93;&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobson1999[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2021]]&lt;sup_class=&quot;noprint_Inline-Template_&quot;_style=&quot;white-space:nowrap;&quot;&gt;&amp;#91;&lt;i&gt;[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|&lt;span_title=&quot;This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&amp;#32;(February_2021)&quot;&gt;page&amp;nbsp;needed&lt;/span&gt;]]&lt;/i&gt;&amp;#93;&lt;/sup&gt;-23">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Septuagint instead used the term "allophuloi" (Î¬Î»Î»ÏÏÏÎ»Î¿Î¹, "other nations") throughout the Books of Judges and Samuel,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoblingRose1996404a_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoblingRose1996404a-26">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Drews49_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Drews49-27">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> such that the term "Philistines" has been interpreted to mean "non-Israelites of the Promised Land" when used in the context of Samson, Saul and David,<sup id="cite_ref-Drews51_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Drews51-28">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and Rabbinic sources explain that these peoples were different from the Philistines of the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Genesis" title="Book of Genesis">Book of Genesis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;vi&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine period</a>, the region of Palestine within <a href="/wiki/Syria_Palaestina" title="Syria Palaestina">Syria Palaestina</a> was subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Prima" title="Palaestina Prima">Palaestina Prima</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Secunda" title="Palaestina Secunda">Secunda</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKaegi199541_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaegi199541-30">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and an area of land including the <a href="/wiki/Negev" title="Negev">Negev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">Sinai</a> became <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Salutaris" title="Palaestina Salutaris">Palaestina Salutaris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKaegi199541_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaegi199541-30">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Levant" title="Muslim conquest of the Levant">Muslim conquest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Place_names_of_Palestine" title="Place names of Palestine">place names</a> that were in use by the Byzantine administration generally continued to be used in Arabic.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESharon19884_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharon19884-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Marshallp559_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marshallp559-31">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The use of the name "Palestine" became common in <a href="/wiki/Early_Modern_English" title="Early Modern English">Early Modern English</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201116_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201116-32">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> was used in English and Arabic during the <a href="/wiki/Mutasarrifate_of_Jerusalem" title="Mutasarrifate of Jerusalem">Mutasarrifate of Jerusalem</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBÃ¼ssow20115_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBÃ¼ssow20115-33">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbu-Manneh199939_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbu-Manneh199939-34">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;vii&#93;</a></sup> and was revived as an official place name with the <a href="/wiki/Mandate_for_Palestine" title="Mandate for Palestine">British Mandate for Palestine</a>.
</p><p>Some other terms that have been used to refer to all or part of this land include <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Israel" title="Land of Israel">Land of Israel</a> (Eretz Yisrael or Ha'aretz),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiger2004133,_159_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiger2004133,_159-37">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;viii&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;ix&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Promised_Land" title="Promised Land">Promised Land</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Syria" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Syria">Greater Syria</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iudaea_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Iudaea Province">Iudaea Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judea" title="Judea">Judea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coele-Syria" title="Coele-Syria">Coele-Syria</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;x&#93;</a></sup> "Israel HaShlema", <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(united_monarchy)" title="Kingdom of Israel (united monarchy)">Kingdom of Israel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">Kingdom of Jerusalem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zion" title="Zion">Zion</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Retjenu" title="Retjenu">Retenu</a></i> (Ancient Egyptian), <a href="/wiki/Southern_Syria" title="Southern Syria">Southern Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Levant" title="Southern Levant">Southern Levant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria_Palaestina" title="Syria Palaestina">Syria Palaestina</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Palestine" title="History of Palestine">History of Palestine</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/Time_periods_in_the_Palestine_region" title="Time periods in the Palestine region">Time periods in the Palestine region</a>.</div>
<p>Situated at a strategic location between <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Syria" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabia">Arabia</a>, and the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, the region has a long and tumultuous history as a crossroads for religion, culture, commerce, and politics. The region has been controlled by numerous peoples, including <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egyptians" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Egyptians">Ancient Egyptians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaanites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">Israelites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Assyrian Empire">Assyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Babylonian Empire">Babylonians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_period#Hellenistic_Middle_east" title="Hellenistic period">Ancient Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a>, the Arab <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">Rashidun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimid</a> <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">caliphates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">Crusaders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ayyubid_dynasty" title="Ayyubid dynasty">Ayyubids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)">Mamluks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongols</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottomans</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a>, and modern <a href="/wiki/Israelis" title="Israelis">Israelis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palestinians" title="Palestinians">Palestinians</a>.
</p>

</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_period">Ancient period</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaan</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_ancient_Israel_and_Judah" title="History of ancient Israel and Judah">History of ancient Israel and Judah</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Philistines" title="Philistines">Philistines</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kingdoms_of_the_Levant_Map_830.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Kingdoms_of_the_Levant_Map_830.png/220px-Kingdoms_of_the_Levant_Map_830.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="262" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Kingdoms_of_the_Levant_Map_830.png/330px-Kingdoms_of_the_Levant_Map_830.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Kingdoms_of_the_Levant_Map_830.png/440px-Kingdoms_of_the_Levant_Map_830.png 2x" data-file-width="1955" data-file-height="2332" /></a><figcaption>Kingdoms of the Southern Levant during the Iron Age (c. 830 BCE)</figcaption></figure>
<p>The region was among the earliest in the world to see human habitation, agricultural communities and <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAhlstrÃ¶m199372â111_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAhlstrÃ¶m199372â111-44">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, independent <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaanite</a> city-states were established, and were influenced by the surrounding civilizations of ancient Egypt, <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minoan_civilization" title="Minoan civilization">Minoan</a> Crete, and Syria. Between 1550 and 1400&#160;BCE, the Canaanite cities became vassals to the Egyptian <a href="/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Egypt" title="New Kingdom of Egypt">New Kingdom</a> who held power until the 1178&#160;BCE <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Djahy" title="Battle of Djahy">Battle of Djahy (Canaan)</a> during the wider <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age_collapse" class="mw-redirect" title="Bronze Age collapse">Bronze Age collapse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAhlstrÃ¶m1993282â334_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAhlstrÃ¶m1993282â334-45">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Israelites" title="Israelites">Israelites</a> emerged from a dramatic social transformation that took place in the people of the central hill country of Canaan around 1200&#160;BCE, with no signs of violent invasion or even of peaceful infiltration of a clearly defined ethnic group from elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFinkelsteinSilberman2002107_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFinkelsteinSilberman2002107-46">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;xi&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a>, the Israelites established two related kingdoms, <a href="/wiki/History_of_ancient_Israel_and_Judah" title="History of ancient Israel and Judah">Israel and Judah</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_(Samaria)" title="Kingdom of Israel (Samaria)">Kingdom of Israel</a> emerged as an important local power by the 10th century BCE before falling to the <a href="/wiki/Neo-Assyrian_Empire" title="Neo-Assyrian Empire">Neo-Assyrian Empire</a> in 722&#160;BCE. Israel's southern neighbor, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah" title="Kingdom of Judah">Kingdom of Judah</a>, emerged in the 8th or 9th century BCE and later became a client state of first the Neo-Assyrian and then the <a href="/wiki/Neo-Babylonian_Empire" title="Neo-Babylonian Empire">Neo-Babylonian Empire</a> before a revolt against the latter led to its destruction in 586&#160;BCE. The region became part of the Neo-Assyrian Empire from c.&#160;740&#160;BCE,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrouch2014_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrouch2014-48">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> which was itself replaced by the Neo-Babylonian Empire in c.&#160;627&#160;BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAhlstrÃ¶m1993655â741,_754â784_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAhlstrÃ¶m1993655â741,_754â784-49">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 587/6&#160;BCE, <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(587_BC)" title="Siege of Jerusalem (587 BC)">Jerusalem was besieged and destroyed</a> by the second Babylonian king, <a href="/wiki/Nebuchadnezzar_II" title="Nebuchadnezzar II">Nebuchadnezzar II</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;xii&#93;</a></sup> who subsequently <a href="/wiki/Babylonian_captivity" title="Babylonian captivity">exiled the Judeans to Babylon</a>. The Kingdom of Judah was then <a href="/wiki/Yehud_(Babylonian_province)" title="Yehud (Babylonian province)">annexed as a Babylonian province</a>. The Philistines were also exiled. The defeat of Judah was recorded by the Babylonians.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBritish_Museumn.d._51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBritish_Museumn.d.-51">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChronicle_of_Nebuchadnezzar_II2006_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChronicle_of_Nebuchadnezzar_II2006-52">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 539&#160;BCE, the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Babylon" title="Fall of Babylon">Babylonian empire was conquered</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible">Hebrew Bible</a> and implications from the <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_Cylinder" title="Cyrus Cylinder">Cyrus Cylinder</a>, the exiled Jews were eventually allowed to <a href="/wiki/The_Return_to_Zion" class="mw-redirect" title="The Return to Zion">return to Jerusalem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAhlstrÃ¶m1993804â890_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAhlstrÃ¶m1993804â890-53">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The returned population in Judah were allowed to self-rule under Persian governance, and some parts of the fallen kingdom became a Persian province known as <a href="/wiki/Yehud_(Persian_province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yehud (Persian province)">Yehud</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrotty201725_f.n._4_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrotty201725_f.n._4-54">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrabbe2004355_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrabbe2004355-55">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Except Yehud, at least another four Persian provinces existed in the region: Samaria, Gaza, Ashdod, and Ascalon, in addition to the Phoenician city states in the north and the Arabian tribes in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEphal2000156_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEphal2000156-56">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> During the same period, the <a href="/wiki/Edom" title="Edom">Edomites</a> migrated from Transjordan to the southern parts of <a href="/wiki/Judea" title="Judea">Judea</a>, which became known as <a href="/wiki/Idumaea" class="mw-redirect" title="Idumaea">Idumaea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevin2020487_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevin2020487-57">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Qedarites" title="Qedarites">Qedarites</a> were the dominant Arab tribe; their territory ran from the <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">Hejaz</a> in the south to the Negev in the north through the period of Persian and Hellenistic dominion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWenning200726:_All_that_can_be_said_with_certainty_is_that_the_Nabataeans_are_known_in_the_sources_since_the_fourth_century_B.C._Up_to_that_time_the_Qedarites,_the_dominant_Arab_tribe_of_the_Persian_period,_controlled_the_south_from_the_Hejaz_and_all_of_the_Negev_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWenning200726:_All_that_can_be_said_with_certainty_is_that_the_Nabataeans_are_known_in_the_sources_since_the_fourth_century_B.C._Up_to_that_time_the_Qedarites,_the_dominant_Arab_tribe_of_the_Persian_period,_controlled_the_south_from_the_Hejaz_and_all_of_the_Negev-58">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_antiquity">Classical antiquity</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:%D7%90%D7%9E%D7%A4%D7%99_%D7%A7%D7%99%D7%A1%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%94.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/%D7%90%D7%9E%D7%A4%D7%99_%D7%A7%D7%99%D7%A1%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%94.jpg/220px-%D7%90%D7%9E%D7%A4%D7%99_%D7%A7%D7%99%D7%A1%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%94.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/%D7%90%D7%9E%D7%A4%D7%99_%D7%A7%D7%99%D7%A1%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%94.jpg/330px-%D7%90%D7%9E%D7%A4%D7%99_%D7%A7%D7%99%D7%A1%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%94.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/%D7%90%D7%9E%D7%A4%D7%99_%D7%A7%D7%99%D7%A1%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%94.jpg/440px-%D7%90%D7%9E%D7%A4%D7%99_%D7%A7%D7%99%D7%A1%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%94.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3992" data-file-height="2992" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Caesarea_Maritima" title="Caesarea Maritima">Caesarea Maritima</a>, also known as Caesarea Palestinae, built under <a href="/wiki/Herod_the_Great" title="Herod the Great">Herod the Great</a> at the site of a former <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenician</a> naval station, became the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Iudaea_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Iudaea Province">Roman Judea</a>, Roman <a href="/wiki/Syria_Palaestina" title="Syria Palaestina">Syria Palaestina</a> and Byzantine <a href="/wiki/Palaestina_Prima" title="Palaestina Prima">Palaestina Prima</a> provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>In the 330s BCE, Macedonian ruler <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> conquered the region, which changed hands several times during the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Diadochi" title="Wars of the Diadochi">wars of the Diadochi</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Wars" title="Syrian Wars">Syrian Wars</a>. It ultimately fell to the <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">Seleucid Empire</a> between 219 and 200&#160;BCE. During that period, the region became heavily <a href="/wiki/Coele-Syria" title="Coele-Syria">hellenized</a>, building tensions between Greeks and locals. In 167&#160;BCE, the <a href="/wiki/Maccabean_Revolt" title="Maccabean Revolt">Maccabean Revolt</a> erupted, leading to the establishment of an independent <a href="/wiki/Hasmonean_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Hasmonean Kingdom">Hasmonean Kingdom</a> in Judea. From 110&#160;BCE, the Hasmoneans extended their authority over much of Palestine, including <a href="/wiki/Samaria" title="Samaria">Samaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">Galilee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iturea" title="Iturea">Iturea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perea" title="Perea">Perea</a>, and Idumea.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith1999210_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith1999210-61">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The Jewish control over the wider region resulted in it also becoming known as <a href="/wiki/Judaea" class="mw-redirect" title="Judaea">Judaea</a>, a term that had previously only referred to the smaller region of the <a href="/wiki/Judaean_Mountains" title="Judaean Mountains">Judaean Mountains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;xiii&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> During the same period, the Edomites were converted to Judaism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevin2020487_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevin2020487-57">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 73 and 63&#160;BCE, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> extended its influence into the region in the <a href="/wiki/Third_Mithridatic_War" title="Third Mithridatic War">Third Mithridatic War</a>. Pompey conquered Judea in 63&#160;BCE, splitting the former Hasmonean Kingdom into five districts. In around 40&#160;BCE, the <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthians</a> conquered Palestine, deposed the Roman ally <a href="/wiki/Hyrcanus_II" title="Hyrcanus II">Hyrcanus II</a>, and installed a puppet ruler of the Hasmonean line known as <a href="/wiki/Antigonus_II_Mattathias" title="Antigonus II Mattathias">Antigonus II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeusner1983911_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeusner1983911-64">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVermes201436_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVermes201436-65">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> By 37&#160;BCE, the Parthians withdrew from Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeusner1983911_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeusner1983911-64">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Palestine is generally considered the "Cradle of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvenari198226_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvenari198226-66">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKÃ¥rtveit2014209_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKÃ¥rtveit2014209-67">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESivan20082_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESivan20082-68">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Christianity, a religion based on the <a href="/wiki/Life_of_Jesus_in_the_New_Testament" class="mw-redirect" title="Life of Jesus in the New Testament">life</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teachings_of_Jesus" class="mw-redirect" title="Teachings of Jesus">teachings</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus of Nazareth</a>, arose as a messianic sect from within <a href="/wiki/Second_Temple_Judaism" title="Second Temple Judaism">Second Temple Judaism</a>. The three-year <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Jesus" title="Ministry of Jesus">Ministry of Jesus</a>, culminating in his <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">crucifixion</a>, is estimated to have occurred from 28 to 30&#160;CE, although the <a href="/wiki/Historicity_of_Jesus" title="Historicity of Jesus">historicity of Jesus</a> is disputed by a minority of scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;xiv&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Second_Temple.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Second_Temple.jpg/220px-Second_Temple.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Second_Temple.jpg/330px-Second_Temple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Second_Temple.jpg/440px-Second_Temple.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a><figcaption>Model of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Temple" title="Second Temple">Second Temple</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>, after being rebuilt by <a href="/wiki/Herod_the_Great" title="Herod the Great">Herod</a>. It was destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> in 70 CE during the <a href="/wiki/First_Jewish%E2%80%93Roman_War" title="First JewishâRoman War">First Jewish-Roman War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Temple_of_Jerusalem&#39;&#39;_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Temple_of_Jerusalem&#39;&#39;-70">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>In the first and second centuries CE, the Province of Judea became the site of two large-scale <a href="/wiki/Jewish%E2%80%93Roman_wars" title="JewishâRoman wars">Jewish revolts against Rome</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/First_Jewish%E2%80%93Roman_War" title="First JewishâRoman War">First Jewish-Roman War</a>, which lasted from 66 to 73&#160;CE, the Romans <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(AD_70)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Jerusalem (AD 70)">razed Jerusalem</a> and destroyed the <a href="/wiki/Second_Temple" title="Second Temple">Second Temple</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZissu201819_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZissu201819-71">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Masada" title="Masada">Masada</a>, Jewish zealots preferred to commit suicide than endure Roman captivity. In 132&#160;CE, another Jewish rebellion erupted. The <a href="/wiki/Bar_Kokhba_revolt" title="Bar Kokhba revolt">Bar Kokhba revolt</a> took three years to put down, incurred massive costs on both the Romans and the Jews, and desolated much of Judea.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewin200533_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewin200533-72">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEshel2008125:_Although_Dio&#39;s_figure_of_985_as_the_number_of_villages_destroyed_during_the_war_seems_hyperbolic,_all_Judaean_villages,_without_exception,_excavated_thus_far_were_razed_following_the_Bar_Kochba_Revolt._This_evidence_supports_the_impression_of_total_regional_destruction_following_the_war._73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEshel2008125:_Although_Dio&#39;s_figure_of_985_as_the_number_of_villages_destroyed_during_the_war_seems_hyperbolic,_all_Judaean_villages,_without_exception,_excavated_thus_far_were_razed_following_the_Bar_Kochba_Revolt._This_evidence_supports_the_impression_of_total_regional_destruction_following_the_war.-73">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The center of Jewish life in Palestine moved to the Galilee.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> During or after the revolt, <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a> joined the province of Iudaea with Galilee and the <a href="/wiki/Paralia_(Palestine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Paralia (Palestine)">Paralia</a> to form the new province of <a href="/wiki/Syria_Palaestina" title="Syria Palaestina">Syria Palaestina</a>, and Jerusalem was renamed "<a href="/wiki/Aelia_Capitolina" title="Aelia Capitolina">Aelia Capitolina</a>". Some scholars view these actions as an attempt to disconnect the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish people">Jewish people</a> from their homeland,<sup id="cite_ref-H.H._Ben-Sasson,_1976,_page_334_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H.H._Ben-Sasson,_1976,_page_334-75">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> but this theory is debated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJacobson199972â74_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJacobson199972â74-21">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 259 and 272, the region fell under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Odaenathus" title="Odaenathus">Odaenathus</a> as King of the <a href="/wiki/Palmyrene_Empire" title="Palmyrene Empire">Palmyrene Empire</a>. Following the victory of Christian emperor <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Civil_wars_of_the_Tetrarchy" title="Civil wars of the Tetrarchy">Civil wars of the Tetrarchy</a>, the Christianization of the Roman Empire began, and in 326, Constantine's mother <a href="/wiki/Helena_(empress)" class="mw-redirect" title="Helena (empress)">Saint Helena</a> visited <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> and began the construction of churches and shrines. Palestine became a center of Christianity, attracting numerous monks and religious scholars. The <a href="/wiki/Samaritan_Revolts" class="mw-redirect" title="Samaritan Revolts">Samaritan Revolts</a> during this period caused their near extinction. In 614&#160;CE, Palestine was annexed by another Persian dynasty; the <a href="/wiki/Sassanids" class="mw-redirect" title="Sassanids">Sassanids</a>, until returning to Byzantine control in 628&#160;CE.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Muslim_period">Early Muslim period</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:294px;max-width:294px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:193px;max-width:193px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Dome_of_Rock,_Temple_Mount,_Jerusalem.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Dome_of_Rock%2C_Temple_Mount%2C_Jerusalem.jpg/191px-Dome_of_Rock%2C_Temple_Mount%2C_Jerusalem.jpg" decoding="async" width="191" height="127" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Dome_of_Rock%2C_Temple_Mount%2C_Jerusalem.jpg/287px-Dome_of_Rock%2C_Temple_Mount%2C_Jerusalem.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Dome_of_Rock%2C_Temple_Mount%2C_Jerusalem.jpg/382px-Dome_of_Rock%2C_Temple_Mount%2C_Jerusalem.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">The <a href="/wiki/Dome_of_the_Rock" title="Dome of the Rock">Dome of the Rock</a>, the world's first great work of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_architecture" title="Islamic architecture">Islamic architecture</a>, constructed in 691.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:97px;max-width:97px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:White_to.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/White_to.jpg/95px-White_to.jpg" decoding="async" width="95" height="127" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/White_to.jpg/143px-White_to.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/White_to.jpg/190px-White_to.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1704" data-file-height="2272" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Minaret of the <a href="/wiki/White_Mosque,_Ramla" class="mw-redirect" title="White Mosque, Ramla">White Mosque</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ramla" title="Ramla">Ramla</a>, constructed in 1318</div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Palestine#Arab_caliphate_period_(640-1099)" title="Architecture of Palestine">Arab architecture in the Umayyad and Mamluk periods</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>Palestine was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">Rashidun Caliphate</a>, beginning in 634&#160;CE.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGil1997i_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGil1997i-78">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> In 636, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Yarmouk" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Yarmouk">Battle of Yarmouk</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Levant" title="Muslim conquest of the Levant">Muslim conquest of the Levant</a> marked the start of Muslim hegemony over the region, which became known as the military district of <a href="/wiki/Jund_Filastin" title="Jund Filastin">Jund Filastin</a> within the province of <a href="/wiki/Bilad_al-Sham" title="Bilad al-Sham">BilÃ¢d al-ShÃ¢m</a> (Greater Syria).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGil199747_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGil199747-79">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In 661, with the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Ali" title="Assassination of Ali">Assassination of Ali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muawiyah_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Muawiyah I">Muawiyah I</a> became the Caliph of the Islamic world after being crowned in Jerusalem.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGil199776_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGil199776-80">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dome_of_the_Rock" title="Dome of the Rock">Dome of the Rock</a>, completed in 691, was the world's first great work of Islamic architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The majority of the population was Christian and was to remain so until the conquest of Saladin in 1187. The Muslim conquest apparently had little impact on social and administrative continuities for several decades.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAvni2014314,_336_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAvni2014314,_336-82">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;xv&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;xvi&#93;</a></sup> The word 'Arab' at the time referred predominantly to Bedouin nomads, though Arab settlement is attested in the Judean highlands and near Jerusalem by the 5th century, and some tribes had converted to Christianity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAvni2014154â155_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAvni2014154â155-86">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The local population engaged in farming, which was considered demeaning, and were called <i>NabaÈ</i>, referring to <a href="/wiki/Aramaic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Aramaic language">Aramaic</a>-speaking villagers. A <a href="/wiki/Hadith" title="Hadith">á¸¥adÄ«th</a>, brought in the name of a Muslim freedman who settled in Palestine, ordered the Muslim Arabs not to settle in the villages, "for he who abides in villages it is as if he abides in graves".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGil1997134â136_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGil1997134â136-87">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyads</a>, who had spurred a strong economic resurgence in the area,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalmsley2000265â343,_p._290_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalmsley2000265â343,_p._290-88">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> were replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasids</a> in 750. <a href="/wiki/Ramla" title="Ramla">Ramla</a> became the administrative centre for the following centuries, while Tiberias became a thriving centre of Muslim scholarship.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGil1997329_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGil1997329-89">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> From 878, Palestine was ruled from Egypt by semi-autonomous rulers for almost a century, beginning with the Turkish freeman <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_ibn_Tulun" title="Ahmad ibn Tulun">Ahmad ibn Tulun</a>, for whom both Jews and Christians prayed when he lay dying<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGil1997306ff._and_p._307_n._71,_p._308_n._73_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGil1997306ff._and_p._307_n._71,_p._308_n._73-90">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> and ending with the <a href="/wiki/Ikhshidid_dynasty" title="Ikhshidid dynasty">Ikhshidid</a> rulers. Reverence for Jerusalem increased during this period, with many of the Egyptian rulers choosing to be buried there.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;xvii&#93;</a></sup> However, the later period became characterized by persecution of Christians as the threat from Byzantium grew.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGil1997324_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGil1997324-92">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimids</a>, with a predominantly <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berber</a> army, conquered the region in 970, a date that marks the beginning of a period of unceasing warfare between numerous enemies, which destroyed Palestine, and in particular, devastating its Jewish population.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGil1997336_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGil1997336-93">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Between 1071 and 1073, Palestine was captured by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Seljuq_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Seljuq Empire">Great Seljuq Empire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGil1997410_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGil1997410-94">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> only to be recaptured by the Fatimids in 1098.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGil1997209,_414_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGil1997209,_414-95">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Crusader.2FAyyubid_period"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Crusader/Ayyubid_period">Crusader/Ayyubid period</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Akko_Castle_30_(5147892579).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Akko_Castle_30_%285147892579%29.jpg/220px-Akko_Castle_30_%285147892579%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Akko_Castle_30_%285147892579%29.jpg/330px-Akko_Castle_30_%285147892579%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Akko_Castle_30_%285147892579%29.jpg/440px-Akko_Castle_30_%285147892579%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Hospitaller</a> fortress in <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a> was destroyed in 1291 and partially rebuilt in the 18th century.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The Fatimids again lost the region to the <a href="/wiki/First_Crusade" title="First Crusade">Crusaders</a> in <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(1099)" title="Siege of Jerusalem (1099)">1099</a>. The Crusaders set up<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">Kingdom of Jerusalem</a> (1099â1291).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGil1997826_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGil1997826-97">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Their control of Jerusalem and most of Palestine lasted almost a century until their <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hattin" title="Battle of Hattin">defeat</a> by <a href="/wiki/Saladin" title="Saladin">Saladin</a>'s forces in 1187,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201115&amp;#32;_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201115&amp;#32;-98">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> after which most of Palestine was controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Ayyubid_dynasty" title="Ayyubid dynasty">Ayyubids</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201115&amp;#32;_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201115&amp;#32;-98">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> except for the years 1229â1244 when Jerusalem and other areas were retaken<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoas200119â20_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoas200119â20-99">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem#The_Kingdom_of_Acre" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">Second Kingdom of Jerusalem</a>, by then ruled from <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a> (1191â1291), but, despite seven further crusades, the Franks were no longer a significant power in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESetton1969615â621_(vol._1)_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESetton1969615â621_(vol._1)-100">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a>, which did not reach Palestine, led directly to the decline of the Byzantine Empire, dramatically reducing Christian influence throughout the region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESetton1969152â185_(vol._2)_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESetton1969152â185_(vol._2)-101">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mamluk_period">Mamluk period</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)">Mamluk Sultanate</a> was created in Egypt as an indirect result of the <a href="/wiki/Seventh_Crusade" title="Seventh Crusade">Seventh Crusade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESetton1969486â518_(vol._2)_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESetton1969486â518_(vol._2)-102">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> reached Palestine for the first time in 1260, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_raids_into_Palestine" title="Mongol raids into Palestine">Mongol raids into Palestine</a> under <a href="/wiki/Nestorian_Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Nestorian Christian">Nestorian Christian</a> general <a href="/wiki/Kitbuqa" title="Kitbuqa">Kitbuqa</a>, and reaching an apex at the pivotal <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ain_Jalut" title="Battle of Ain Jalut">Battle of Ain Jalut</a>, where they were pushed back by the Mamluks.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201135â39_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201135â39-103">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_period">Ottoman period</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Palestine#Ottoman_period" title="History of Palestine">History of Palestine Â§&#160;Ottoman period</a></div>
<p>In 1486, hostilities broke out between the Mamluks and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in a battle for control over western Asia, and the Ottomans conquered Palestine in 1516.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201140_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201140-104">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Between the mid-16th and 17th centuries, a close-knit alliance of three local dynasties, the <a href="/wiki/Ridwan_dynasty" title="Ridwan dynasty">Ridwans</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Al-Lajjun#Early_rule_and_the_Tarabay_family" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Lajjun">Turabays</a> of <a href="/wiki/Al-Lajjun" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Lajjun">al-Lajjun</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Farrukh_Pasha#Legacy" title="Farrukh Pasha">Farrukhs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nablus" title="Nablus">Nablus</a>, governed Palestine on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Sublime_Porte" title="Sublime Porte">Porte</a> (imperial Ottoman government).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZeevi199645_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZeevi199645-105">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Akko_BW_13.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Akko_BW_13.JPG/220px-Akko_BW_13.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Akko_BW_13.JPG/330px-Akko_BW_13.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Akko_BW_13.JPG/440px-Akko_BW_13.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3373" data-file-height="2460" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Khan_al-Umdan" title="Khan al-Umdan">Khan al-Umdan</a>, constructed in <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a> in 1784, is the largest and best preserved <a href="/wiki/Caravanserai" title="Caravanserai">caravanserai</a> in the region.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In the 18th century, the <a href="/wiki/Al-Zayadina" title="Al-Zayadina">Zaydani</a> clan under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Zahir_al-Umar" title="Zahir al-Umar">Zahir al-Umar</a> ruled large parts of Palestine autonomously<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhillipp201342â43_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhillipp201342â43-106">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> until the Ottomans were able to defeat them in their <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">Galilee</a> strongholds in 1775â76.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoudah1987115â117_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoudah1987115â117-107">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Zahir had turned the port city of <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a> into a major regional power, partly fueled by his monopolization of the <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a> trade from Palestine to Europe. Acre's regional dominance was further elevated under Zahir's successor <a href="/wiki/Jazzar_Pasha" title="Jazzar Pasha">Ahmad Pasha al-Jazzar</a> at the expense of <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurns2005246_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurns2005246-108">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1830, on the eve of <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt" title="Muhammad Ali of Egypt">Muhammad Ali</a>'s invasion,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201164_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201164-109">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> the Porte transferred control of the sanjaks of Jerusalem and Nablus to <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_Pasha_ibn_Ali" title="Abdullah Pasha ibn Ali">Abdullah Pasha</a>, the governor of Acre. According to Silverburg, in regional and cultural terms this move was important for creating an Arab Palestine detached from greater Syria (<i>bilad al-Sham</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESilverburg20099â36,_p._29_n._32_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESilverburg20099â36,_p._29_n._32-110">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> According to Pappe, it was an attempt to reinforce the Syrian front in face of Muhammad Ali's invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPappe199938_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPappe199938-111">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Two years later, Palestine was conquered by Muhammad Ali's Egypt,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201164_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201164-109">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> but Egyptian rule was challenged in 1834 by a <a href="/wiki/Peasants%27_Revolt_of_1834_(Palestine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Peasants&#39; Revolt of 1834 (Palestine)">countrywide popular uprising</a> against <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> and other measures considered intrusive by the population.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKimmerlingMigdal20037â8_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKimmerlingMigdal20037â8-112">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Its suppression devastated many of Palestine's villages and major towns.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKimmerlingMigdal200311_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKimmerlingMigdal200311-113">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1840, Britain intervened and returned control of the Levant to the Ottomans in return for further <a href="/wiki/Capitulations_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Capitulations of the Ottoman Empire">capitulations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201171_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer201171-114">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The death of <a href="/wiki/Aqil_Agha" title="Aqil Agha">Aqil Agha</a> marked the last local challenge to Ottoman centralization in Palestine,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYazbak19983_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYazbak19983-115">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> and beginning in the 1860s, Palestine underwent an acceleration in its socio-economic development, due to its incorporation into the global, and particularly European, economic pattern of growth. The beneficiaries of this process were Arabic-speaking Muslims and Christians who emerged as a new layer within the Arab elite.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbar1986188_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbar1986188-116">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> From 1880 large-scale Jewish immigration began, almost entirely from Europe, based on an explicitly <a href="/wiki/Zionist" class="mw-redirect" title="Zionist">Zionist</a> ideology.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJVLn.d._117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJVLn.d.-117">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2022)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> There was also a <a href="/wiki/Revival_of_the_Hebrew_language" title="Revival of the Hebrew language">revival of the Hebrew language and culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;xviii&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Christian_Zionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Christian Zionism in the United Kingdom">Christian Zionism in the United Kingdom</a> preceded its spread within the Jewish community.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShapira201415_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShapira201415-119">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The government of Great Britain publicly supported it during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration" title="Balfour Declaration">Balfour Declaration</a> of 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer2011148_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKrÃ¤mer2011148-120">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_mandate_and_partition">British mandate and partition</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine" title="Mandatory Palestine">Mandatory Palestine</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Zionism" title="Zionism">Zionism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_nationalism" title="Palestinian nationalism">Palestinian nationalism</a></div>
